Your task:  "positive-kernel / repeated-source monotonicity route at the source level"

We are trying to prove the Riemann Hypothesis. Please see attached paper draft.

Current status, in one paragraph:

On the **nonmixed (4)-point side**, the local derivative-geometry story is essentially finished. Exact nonmixed contacts force zeros of (\mathcal R); one-sign (\mathcal R)-intervals are sterile; recurrent exact contacts force affine-planar collapse; isolated zeros of (\mathcal R) are classified by parity; and the repeated-source / first-loss mechanism is now fully reduced: first loss occurs **iff** one diagonally approaches an odd zero of (\mathcal R). So there is no separate first-loss obstruction left beyond odd-zero birth. Equivalently, on a nonmixed arc the whole burden is to exclude odd zeros of the source-level Wronskian
[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'.
]
At the same time, two no-go results are now clear: the current (3)-point package for the original planar curve ((x,S)) does **not** by itself contradict the sheared repeated-node tangent-contact event, and the current source-level ratio/Wronskian/(4\times4)-Wronskian package is still formally too free. So the missing ingredient is now a genuine **source-coupling / shear-transfer theorem**, not more local parity analysis. The repeated-source lane is closed cleanly by the theorem that first loss is exactly diagonal odd-zero birth.

Your task:  "positive-kernel / repeated-source monotonicity route at the source level"

Read the latest draft and work only on the repeated-source / monotonicity formulation. The key objects are:
[
\Gamma_a(x)=
\frac{Y(x)-Y(a)-Y'(a)(x-a)}
{S(x)-S(a)-S'(a)(x-a)},
\qquad
\Psi_a(h)=\frac{D_{u_5}(a,h)}{D_\lambda(a,h)},
]
and the determinant (\mathfrak D(a,h)) controlling the source-level derivative. The repeated-source lane is now fully classified locally: first loss occurs iff one diagonally approaches an odd zero of (\mathcal R). So there is no separate first-loss mechanism left. What remains is to show that on a **genuine opened nonmixed arc**, the needed first odd zero / monotonicity loss cannot occur.

Your task is to push the **positive-kernel / source-determinant** route as far as possible. I want one of the following:

* a one-sign theorem for (\Gamma_a'), (\Psi_a'), or (\mathfrak D(a,h)) near the diagonal on opened nonmixed arcs;
* a theorem that the first odd zero of (\mathcal R) would force a forbidden sign change or variation property for the family (\Gamma_a) or (\Psi_a);
* or a reduction of odd-zero birth to a concrete sign contradiction for (\mathfrak D(a,h)).

Please assume the theorem that repeated-source first loss is exactly diagonal odd-zero birth, and do **not** spend time reproving that classification. The goal here is not local birth theory, but a **global monotonicity / sign exclusion** for the realized family (\Gamma_a), (\Psi_a), or (\mathfrak D(a,h)) on genuine opened nonmixed arcs.

I’m going into the draft to isolate the exact source-level identities around ΓaΓa​, ΨaΨa​, D(a,h)D(a,h), and the nonmixed/opened hypotheses, then I’ll see whether they support an actual sign theorem or only a conditional reduction.

I’ve got the key section. The good news is the draft already contains the exact positive-kernel representation and the source-determinant lift, so the remaining work is to squeeze a real variation theorem out of that kernel rather than invent a new object.

I think there is a real theorem available here.

The strongest thing I can get from the current kernel machinery is not a full one-sign theorem for Γa′Γa′​ or DD on all opened nonmixed arcs, but a sharper obstruction:

    a segment that sees only one sign change of RR cannot support the rigidified first-loss event.

That is exactly the positive-kernel/source-determinant route, pushed one step beyond what is already in the draft.

Γa​(x)−Z(a).

Da(t)=∫01(1−s) Y~′′(a+s(t−a)) ds,Da(a)=Z(a),

so

2. The actual theorem

Let
k1(s):=s(1−s),k0(s):=(1−s)2.
k1​(s):=s(1−s),k0​(s):=(1−s)2.

Then
k0(s)k1(s)=1−ss,
k1​(s)k0​(s)​=s1−s​,

which is strictly decreasing on (0,1)(0,1).

That gives:
Single-sign-change extremum theorem.
Single-sign-change extremum theorem.​

Assume a<xa<x lie on an opened nonmixed arc, and assume that
Γa′(x)=0.
Γa′​(x)=0.

Suppose moreover that RR has exactly one sign change on (a,x)(a,x).

Then
sgn⁡(Γa(x)−Z(a))
sgn(Γa​(x)−Z(a))

is forced: it equals the sign of RR on the initial side of the interval (a,x)(a,x). In particular,
Γa(x)≠Z(a).
Γa​(x)=Z(a).

So a segment with exactly one sign change of RR can produce a repeated-source extremum, but it can never satisfy the rigidified first-loss balance.
Proof idea

Write Ra,x(s)=σ(s)ρ(s)Ra,x​(s)=σ(s)ρ(s) with ρ≥0ρ≥0 and σσ changing sign exactly once.
From Γa′(x)=0Γa′​(x)=0,
∫01k1(s)σ(s)ρ(s) ds=0.
∫01​k1​(s)σ(s)ρ(s)ds=0.

Then
Γa(x)−Z(a)∝∫01k0(s)σ(s)ρ(s) ds=∫01k0k1(s) k1(s)σ(s)ρ(s) ds.
Γa​(x)−Z(a)∝∫01​k0​(s)σ(s)ρ(s)ds=∫01​k1​k0​​(s)k1​(s)σ(s)ρ(s)ds.

Because k0/k1k0​/k1​ is strictly decreasing, it is larger on the earlier-sign side than on the later-sign side. Once the k1k1​-weighted masses balance, the k0k0​-weighted integral keeps the sign of the earlier side. Hence it cannot vanish.
3. What this gives at source level

Since
Ψa(h)=Γx(a)(x(h)),Ψa′(h)∼D(a,h),
Ψa​(h)=Γx(a)​(x(h)),Ψa′​(h)∼D(a,h),

the same statement becomes:

    If Ψa′(h)=0Ψa′​(h)=0 and the pulled-back source-level scalar WsrcWsrc​ changes sign exactly once on the source segment from aa to hh, then
    Ψa(h)−Z(a)
    Ψa​(h)−Z(a)

    has a forced nonzero sign. Therefore
    Ψa′(h)=0,Ψa(h)=Z(a)
    Ψa′​(h)=0,Ψa​(h)=Z(a)

    cannot occur simultaneously.

Equivalently:
Any realized first-loss segment must cross at least two sign changes of R (hence of Wsrc).
Any realized first-loss segment must cross at least two sign changes of R (hence of Wsrc​).​

That is the cleanest monotonicity/sign reduction I can get from the current source-determinant framework.
4. What it does and does not close

What it does show:

    a lone first odd zero is not enough to satisfy the full rigidified first-loss balance on any fixed segment;

    the repeated-source obstruction is now at least a two-sign-change phenomenon at the kernel level, not a one-sign-change phenomenon.

What it does not yet show:

    it does not exclude the local derivative-zero branch born at an odd zero;

    so it does not by itself kill odd-zero birth.

But it materially tightens the burden:

    the missing source-coupling theorem no longer has to rule out every local odd-zero extremum directly; it is enough to rule out the additional oscillation needed to turn that local extremum mechanism into a genuine first-loss segment.

That is a real reduction.
5. The crisp proposition to add

Here is the theorem in paper-style math form.

\begin{proposition}[Single-sign-change source segment cannot realize rigidified first loss]
\label{prop:single-sign-change-cannot-realize-first-loss}
Let $J$ be an opened nonmixed arc, and let $a<x$ in $J$.
After local nonmixed normalization on $[a,x]$, write
\[
R_{a,x}(s):=\mathcal R(a+s(x-a)),
\qquad 0\le s\le 1.
\]
Then
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)
=
2\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_{a,x}(s)\,ds,
\]
and
\[
\Gamma_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)
=
(x-a)\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_{a,x}(s)\,ds.
\]

Assume that $R_{a,x}$ has exactly one sign change on $(0,1)$.
If
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)=0,
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(\Gamma_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
\]
is the sign of $R_{a,x}$ on the initial side of the sign change.
In particular,
\[
\Gamma_a(x)\neq \mathcal Z(a).
\]

Equivalently, no pair $(a,x)$ for which $\mathcal R$ changes sign exactly once
on $(a,x)$ can satisfy simultaneously
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_a(x)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
Hence any rigidified first-loss segment must cross at least two sign changes of
$\mathcal R$.
\end{proposition}

And the source-level corollary is:

\begin{corollary}[Source-level two-sign-change obstruction]
\label{cor:source-level-two-sign-change-obstruction}
Let $a<h$ lie on an opened nonmixed arc in source coordinates.
Assume
\[
\Psi_a'(h)=0.
\]
If the source-level Wronskian
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
\]
changes sign exactly once on the source interval $[a,h]$, then
\[
\Psi_a(h)\neq \mathcal Z(a).
\]
Equivalently, the simultaneous source-level first-loss conditions
\[
\Psi_a'(h)=0,
\qquad
\Psi_a(h)=\mathcal Z(a)
\]
force at least two sign changes of $\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}$ on $[a,h]$.
\end{corollary}

This is the best honest push I see from the positive-kernel / source-determinant lane with the current draft.

The next useful push is to stop looking only at the kernel average
Γa′(x)∼∫Ωa,x R
Γa′​(x)∼∫Ωa,x​R

and instead package it as a triple primitive of RR on each normalized nonmixed segment. That gives a stronger “one-sign-change chamber” theorem.

After local nonmixed normalization S(t)=t2S(t)=t2, write Da=ΓaDa​=Γa​. Then the draft already gives

Da′​(x)=2∫01​s(1−s)R(a+s(x−a))ds.

From the same calculation one also gets the two endpoint-gap identities
Da(x)−Z(a)=(x−a)∫01(1−s)2 R(a+s(x−a)) ds,
Da​(x)−Z(a)=(x−a)∫01​(1−s)2R(a+s(x−a))ds,

and
Z(x)−Da(x)=(x−a)∫01s2 R(a+s(x−a)) ds.
Z(x)−Da​(x)=(x−a)∫01​s2R(a+s(x−a))ds.

That is already stronger than the earlier moment argument, because now at any critical pair Da′(x)=0Da′​(x)=0, the three weights
s(1−s),(1−s)2,s2
s(1−s),(1−s)2,s2

can be compared directly.

If RR has exactly one sign change on (a,x)(a,x), then:
sgn⁡(Da(x)−Z(a))=sign of the initial lobe of R,
sgn(Da​(x)−Z(a))=sign of the initial lobe of R,

while
sgn⁡(Z(x)−Da(x))=sign of the terminal lobe of R.
sgn(Z(x)−Da​(x))=sign of the terminal lobe of R.

So a one-sign-change critical point does not just fail the rigidified first-loss condition Da(x)=Z(a)Da​(x)=Z(a). It actually satisfies the stronger endpoint-separation law:

    if RR is ++ then −− on (a,x)(a,x), then
    Da(x)>Z(a)andDa(x)>Z(x);
    Da​(x)>Z(a)andDa​(x)>Z(x);

    if RR is −− then ++, then
    Da(x)<Z(a)andDa(x)<Z(x).
    Da​(x)<Z(a)andDa​(x)<Z(x).

So the critical value lies strictly outside the endpoint-curvature interval. That is better than the earlier “not equal to Z(a)Z(a)” statement.

The really useful reformulation is this:
Fa(x):=(x−a)32 Da′(x)=∫ax(r−a)(x−r) R(r) dr.
Fa​(x):=2(x−a)3​Da′​(x)=∫ax​(r−a)(x−r)R(r)dr.

Then
Fa′(x)=∫ax(r−a) R(r) dr,Fa′′(x)=∫axR(r) dr=Z(x)−Z(a),Fa′′′(x)=R(x).
Fa′​(x)=∫ax​(r−a)R(r)dr,Fa′′​(x)=∫ax​R(r)dr=Z(x)−Z(a),Fa′′′​(x)=R(x).

That is the key extra step.

Because Fa′′′Fa′′′​ is just RR, if RR has exactly one sign change on a chamber, then Fa′′Fa′′​ is unimodal, Fa′Fa′​ has at most one turning point, and FaFa​ has at most one positive zero. So for fixed aa:

    on any interval where the segment [a,x][a,x] sees exactly one sign change of RR, the equation Da′(x)=0Da′​(x)=0 has at most one solution.

And that zero, if it exists, is simple. Indeed, at Da′(x)=0Da′​(x)=0,
Fa′(x)=(x−a)(Z(x)−Da(x)),
Fa′​(x)=(x−a)(Z(x)−Da​(x)),

so by the endpoint-separation law it has the sign of the terminal lobe of RR, hence is nonzero.

This gives a clean geometric picture of the repeated-source branch in a one-sign-change chamber:

    for each anchor aa, there is at most one target xx with Da′(x)=0Da′​(x)=0;

    the zero is transverse;

    the critical branch is harmless there in the sense that it cannot satisfy the rigidified first-loss equality Da(x)=Z(a)Da​(x)=Z(a);

    so a locally born odd-zero branch cannot produce genuine first-loss behavior until the segment picks up a second sign change of RR.

That last sentence is probably the best honest “further push” from this route:

    odd-zero birth is not enough; to participate in actual monotonicity loss, the born critical branch must survive until a second sign change of RR appears on the segment.

At source level this translates directly through
Ψa(h)=Γx(a)(x(h)),D(a,h)∼Dx(a)′(x(h)).
Ψa​(h)=Γx(a)​(x(h)),D(a,h)∼Dx(a)′​(x(h)).

So on a source interval where WsrcWsrc​ has exactly one sign change, for each source anchor aa there is at most one hh with D(a,h)=0D(a,h)=0, that zero is simple, and it cannot realize the rigidified first-loss balance. Any genuine nonmixed obstruction must therefore span at least two sign changes of WsrcWsrc​.

I do not think the positive-kernel route alone gets all the way to contradiction from here. But it does sharpen the burden substantially. The remaining theorem is no longer “kill odd-zero birth.” It is:

    show that on a genuine opened nonmixed arc, the source-level Wronskian cannot supply the second oscillation needed to turn a locally born repeated-source critical branch into an actual first-loss mechanism.

That feels like a real reduction, not just repackaging.

Yes. I think the next real step is a transport theorem for the born critical branch. It pushes the positive-kernel route further than the earlier “two sign changes are needed” statement.

That gives a much sharper statement than before:

    On any chamber where the critical segment sees exactly one sign change of RR, the born critical branch has strictly negative slope, stays simple, and its critical value lies strictly outside the endpoint-curvature interval [Z(a),Z(τ(a))][Z(a),Z(τ(a))].

That is the clean “no-return in the one-sign-change chamber” theorem.

The next structural consequence is this.

Take the odd-zero birth branch coming from an isolated odd zero bb of RR. Let II be the maximal interval of continuation on which every segment [a,τ(a)][a,τ(a)] contains exactly that one sign change. On II, the branch is analytic, simple, and τ′(a)<0τ′(a)<0. So the only way it can ever leave that chamber is if the sign-change count of RR on [a,τ(a)][a,τ(a)] changes. For an analytic fixed RR, that can only happen when a zero of RR crosses an endpoint of the segment. Since the branch stays simple inside the chamber, there is no internal catastrophe available before that.

So you get:
Any global obstruction branch issued from an odd zero b must continue until one endpoint hits a second zero c≠b of R.
Any global obstruction branch issued from an odd zero b must continue until one endpoint hits a second zero c=b of R.​

    D(a,h)=0,
    D(a,h)=0,

    equivalently Ψa′(h)=0Ψa′​(h)=0;

    on the chamber where the source segment [a,h][a,h] sees exactly one sign change of
    Wsrc,
    Wsrc​,

    the branch has strictly negative slope in the induced xx-coordinate and cannot satisfy
    Ψa(h)=Z(a);
    Ψa​(h)=Z(a);

    therefore any genuine nonmixed obstruction branch must connect one odd zero of WsrcWsrc​ to a second zero of WsrcWsrc​.

That is the strongest honest push I can get from the positive-kernel/source-determinant route alone.

What I do not see from the current draft is a way to rule out that second-zero connection purely by generic kernel algebra. The present machinery seems to reduce the problem to a very concrete target:

    zero-connection exclusion for the source-level Wronskian branch.

That feels like the right next theorem to try to prove.

Yes. Here are the exact insertions I would make.

The main new block should go immediately after Corollary~\ref{cor:source-level-two-sign-change-obstruction} and before \begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed $4$-point side].

\begin{proposition}[Transport equations for a repeated-source critical branch]
\label{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}
Let $J$ be an opened nonmixed arc, and work in a local normalized nonmixed
chart on which
\[
S(t)=t^2,
\qquad
\Gamma_a=D_a.
\]
Let $U\subset J$ be an interval, and let
\[
\tau:U\to J
\]
be a real-analytic function such that
\[
\tau(a)>a,
\qquad
D_a'(\tau(a))=0
\qquad (a\in U).
\]
Set
\[
V(a):=D_a(\tau(a)).
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
V'(a)=\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a}\,\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]

\item
\[
D_a''(\tau(a))
=
\frac{2}{(\tau(a)-a)^2}\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr).
\]

\item
At any point $a\in U$ where $D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0$,
\[
\tau'(a)
=
\frac{V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)}
{\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
D_a(t)
=
\frac{\widetilde Y(t)-\widetilde Y(a)-\widetilde Y'(a)(t-a)}{(t-a)^2}.
\]
Differentiating in $a$ gives
\[
\partial_a D_a(t)
=
\frac{2}{t-a}\,\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]
Evaluating at $t=\tau(a)$ and using $D_a'(\tau(a))=0$ yields
\[
V'(a)
=
\frac{d}{da}D_a(\tau(a))
=
\partial_a D_a(\tau(a))
=
\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a}\,\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr),
\]
which proves (1).

Now use the rigidification scalar
\[
M(a,t):=B_a(t)^2\,\Gamma_a'(t).
\]
In the normalized chart,
\[
B_a(t)=(t-a)^2,
\qquad
\Gamma_a=D_a,
\qquad
M(a,t)=(t-a)^4\,D_a'(t).
\]
By Remark~\ref{rem:first-loss-rigidification-nonmixed},
\[
\partial_t M(a,t)
=
2(t-a)^2\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(t)-D_a(t)\bigr).
\]
At $t=\tau(a)$ we have $D_a'(\tau(a))=0$, so
\[
\partial_t M(a,\tau(a))
=
(\tau(a)-a)^4\,D_a''(\tau(a)).
\]
Comparing the two formulas gives
\[
(\tau(a)-a)^4\,D_a''(\tau(a))
=
2(\tau(a)-a)^2\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr),
\]
hence (2).

Finally, still by Remark~\ref{rem:first-loss-rigidification-nonmixed},
at points where $M(a,t)=0$ one has
\[
\partial_a M(a,t)
=
2(t-a)^2\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(a)-D_a(t)\bigr),
\]
in the normalized chart. Since
\[
M(a,\tau(a))=0,
\]
differentiating in $a$ gives
\[
0=\frac{d}{da}M(a,\tau(a))
=
\partial_a M(a,\tau(a))
+
\partial_t M(a,\tau(a))\,\tau'(a).
\]
Substituting the formulas above yields
\[
0
=
2(\tau(a)-a)^2\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(a)-V(a)\bigr)
+
2(\tau(a)-a)^2\,\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr)\tau'(a).
\]
If $D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0$, then by (2),
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\neq 0,
\]
so solving for $\tau'(a)$ gives (3).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[One-sign-change chamber is no-return for the born critical branch]
\label{cor:one-sign-change-chamber-no-return}
In the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch},
assume moreover that for every $a\in U$ the segment
\[
[a,\tau(a)]
\]
contains exactly one sign change of $\mathcal R$.

Then for every $a\in U$:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
\]
is the sign of the initial lobe of $\mathcal R$ on $[a,\tau(a)]$;

\item
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr)
\]
is the sign of the terminal lobe of $\mathcal R$ on $[a,\tau(a)]$;

\item
\[
\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr)<0;
\]

\item
\[
D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0,
\qquad
\tau'(a)<0;
\]

\item
\[
V(a)\notin [\,\mathcal Z(a),\mathcal Z(\tau(a))\,].
\]
In particular,
\[
V(a)\neq \mathcal Z(a),
\]
so the branch cannot realize the rigidified first-loss condition anywhere on
$U$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The first sign statement is exactly
Proposition~\ref{prop:single-sign-change-cannot-realize-first-loss} applied to
the critical pair $(a,\tau(a))$.

For the second sign statement, write
\[
R_{a,\tau(a)}(s):=\mathcal R(a+s(\tau(a)-a)).
\]
Since
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)
=
(\tau(a)-a)\int_0^1 R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds
\]
and
\[
V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)
=
(\tau(a)-a)\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds,
\]
one gets
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)
=
(\tau(a)-a)\int_0^1 (2s-s^2)\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds.
\]
At the critical pair,
\[
0=D_a'(\tau(a))
=
2\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds,
\]
so
\[
\int_0^1 (2s-s^2)\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds
=
\int_0^1 s^2\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds.
\]
Hence
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)
=
(\tau(a)-a)\int_0^1 s^2\,R_{a,\tau(a)}(s)\,ds.
\]
Now set
\[
k_1(s):=s(1-s),
\qquad
k_2(s):=s^2.
\]
Then
\[
\frac{k_2(s)}{k_1(s)}=\frac{s}{1-s}
\]
is strictly increasing on $(0,1)$. Repeating the weighted signed-mass argument
from the proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:single-sign-change-cannot-realize-first-loss} shows that
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)\bigr)
\]
is the sign of the terminal lobe of $\mathcal R$.

The two signs are therefore opposite, which proves (3). Then
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(2)
gives
\[
D_a''(\tau(a))\neq 0,
\]
and
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(3)
gives
\[
\tau'(a)<0.
\]
Finally, opposite signs of
\[
V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)
\]
mean exactly that $V(a)$ lies strictly outside the endpoint-curvature interval
\[
[\,\mathcal Z(a),\mathcal Z(\tau(a))\,].
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Zero-connection reduction for the repeated-source branch]
\label{rem:zero-connection-reduction-repeated-source}
Let $b$ be an isolated odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$, and let
\[
t=\tau(a)
\]
denote the local born repeated-source critical branch supplied by
Proposition~\ref{prop:parity-classification-isolated-nonmixed-R-zeros}.
On any maximal continuation interval on which each segment
\[
[a,\tau(a)]
\]
contains exactly one sign change of $\mathcal R$,
Corollary~\ref{cor:one-sign-change-chamber-no-return} shows that the branch
remains simple, satisfies
\[
\tau'(a)<0,
\]
and cannot realize the rigidified first-loss condition
\[
D_a(\tau(a))=\mathcal Z(a).
\]

Thus the only internal way for such a branch to leave the one-sign-change
chamber is for the sign-change count on the segment to change; for analytic
$\mathcal R$, this occurs only when an endpoint of the segment meets another
zero of $\mathcal R$ (equivalently, unless the branch exits the local chart or
the opened arc). Via
Remark~\ref{rem:source-determinant-reformulation-Gammaa},
the same statement holds at source level for a local branch of
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0.
\]
Accordingly, any genuine repeated-source obstruction branch must either leave
the nonmixed chart/arc or connect one odd zero of
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
\]
to a second zero of $\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}$.
\end{remark}

anything more we can do on this line of attack?

Yes. There is at least one more genuine reduction on this line, and one important sharpening.

The sharpening is this: everywhere we’ve been saying “second zero,” the right phrase is really second sign-changing zero, i.e. second odd zero of RR (equivalently of WsrcWsrc​). An even zero does not change the sign-change count on the segment, so it does not break the one-sign-change chamber.

That lets you push the current line one step further.

The clean theorem is:
If an opened nonmixed arc contains at most one odd zero of R, then repeated-source first loss is impossible on that arc.
If an opened nonmixed arc contains at most one odd zero of R, then repeated-source first loss is impossible on that arc.​

Why this is true:

    if there is no odd zero, there is no birth mechanism at all;

    if there is one odd zero bb, any born repeated-source critical branch stays in the one-sign-change chamber for as long as the segment remains in the arc, because no second odd zero can enter the segment;

    on that chamber, your new transport/no-return theorem applies: the branch is simple, has τ′(a)<0τ′(a)<0, and cannot satisfy the rigidified first-loss equality.

So the remaining nonmixed repeated-source problem is not “exclude odd zeros on opened arcs” in full generality anymore. It is narrower:
exclude a branch connecting one odd zero of R to a second odd zero of R.
exclude a branch connecting one odd zero of R to a second odd zero of R.​

And you can sharpen that again.

Order the odd zeros on the arc by position:
b1<b2<⋯<bm.
b1​<b2​<⋯<bm​.

Then any genuine obstruction branch can only involve adjacent odd zeros in this order. It cannot skip an odd zero, because the first time the one-sign-change chamber can fail is exactly when the segment first picks up another sign change, and that first extra sign change comes from the nearest odd zero on the expanding side.

So the line of attack reduces all the way to a nearest-neighbor odd-zero connection problem.

That is a real improvement. It means the minimal bad configuration is no longer some vague global oscillation of WsrcWsrc​; it is this:

    there exist two adjacent odd zeros b<cb<c of RR on a genuine opened nonmixed arc, and a repeated-source critical branch born at bb survives all the way until the segment first reaches cc.

That is the first configuration not already excluded by the current kernel/transport machinery.

I would formulate the next theorem target exactly that way:
Adjacent-odd-zero exclusion.A born repeated-source critical branch cannot continue from one odd zeroof R to the next odd zero on a genuine opened nonmixed arc.
Adjacent-odd-zero exclusion.A born repeated-source critical branch cannot continue from one odd zeroof R to the next odd zero on a genuine opened nonmixed arc.​

That is now the right bottleneck for this line.

There is also a modest draft correction I would make if you insert the current remarks: change “second zero” to “second odd zero” or “second sign-changing zero” in the zero-connection remark. That makes the reduction sharper and more correct.

If you want, I can give you the exact LaTeX insertions for:

    the “at most one odd zero implies sterility” proposition,

    the “adjacent odd zero reduction” corollary,

    and the wording fixes replacing “second zero” by “second odd zero / sign-changing zero.”

\begin{proposition}[At most one odd zero implies no genuine repeated-source obstruction]
\label{prop:at-most-one-odd-zero-no-genuine-repeated-source-obstruction}
Let $J$ be an opened nonmixed arc. Assume that $\mathcal R$ has at most one
odd-order zero on $J$. Then there is no pair $a<x$ in $J$ such that
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_a(x)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
Equivalently, there is no source-level pair $a<h$ on the corresponding source
arc such that
\[
\Psi_a'(h)=0,
\qquad
\Psi_a(h)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
On a nonmixed arc, $\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}$ differs from $\mathcal R$ only
by a nonvanishing analytic factor
(Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point}), so odd
zeros and sign changes of the two objects coincide.

If $\mathcal R$ has at most one odd-order zero on $J$, then every segment
contained in $J$ contains at most one sign change of $\mathcal R$ (equivalently
of $\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}$), since even-order zeros do not change sign.
Hence Corollary~\ref{cor:source-level-two-sign-change-obstruction} excludes any
simultaneous source-level solution of
\[
\Psi_a'(h)=0,
\qquad
\Psi_a(h)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
Via Remark~\ref{rem:source-determinant-reformulation-Gammaa}, this is
equivalent to the planar formulation
\[
\Gamma_a'(x)=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_a(x)=\mathcal Z(a).
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Minimal unresolved configuration on this route]
\label{rem:minimal-unresolved-configuration-repeated-source}
Proposition~\ref{prop:at-most-one-odd-zero-no-genuine-repeated-source-obstruction}
shows that the positive-kernel / source-determinant route has already ruled out
every opened nonmixed arc carrying at most one odd zero of $\mathcal R}$.
Accordingly, the first unresolved configuration on this route is no longer a
single odd-zero birth, but an arc carrying at least two odd zeros of
$\mathcal R$.

In particular, the minimal genuinely live scenario is a repeated-source
critical branch born at one odd zero of $\mathcal R$ and continuing until the
segment acquires the next odd zero. Thus the sharpened source-coupling target
is an adjacent-odd-zero connection exclusion theorem on genuine opened
nonmixed arcs.
\end{remark}

I would say: basically done as a free-standing branch, but not fully dead.

More precisely, I think the current positive-kernel / monotonicity route has been pushed to its natural frontier. It has already given the useful reductions:

    first loss is not a separate mechanism;

As a sharply targeted theorem: there is still one live attack left.

That live target is:
adjacent odd-zero connection exclusion
adjacent odd-zero connection exclusion​

Namely: prove that a repeated-source critical branch born at one odd zero of RR cannot continue all the way until the segment first reaches the next odd zero.

That is the one remaining theorem on this line that would actually move the proof.

If you want to keep attacking this branch, I would only do it in one of these very specific ways:

First, a minimal bad pair argument. Assume a counterexample and choose the first anchor aa for which the born branch reaches a second odd zero. Then try to derive a contradiction from first-contact geometry at that endpoint. This is the cleanest remaining attack within the present framework.

Second, a branch transport plus endpoint asymptotics attack. Use the formulas for V′(a)V′(a) and τ′(a)τ′(a), and study what must happen as the moving endpoint approaches the second odd zero. If one can show the required limiting behavior of V(a)V(a) is incompatible with the local odd-zero model at the target endpoint, that would close the branch.

Third, a new structural input at source level: some total-positivity, variation-diminishing, or Sturm/Chebyshev-type fact for the realized family. Without something like that, I doubt the current kernel identities alone will kill the two-odd-zero connection.

So my recommendation would be:

    treat this branch as reduced to one precise bottleneck;

    stop broad exploration here;

    either attack the adjacent odd-zero connection theorem directly,

Holistically: no, the draft does not yet solve the two-odd-zero issue.

But it does isolate it very sharply, and it points to a fairly specific next direction.

What the draft now says, taken together, is:

The current generic source-level algebra is not enough.
That is exactly what Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-package-not-enough} says: the ratio/Wronskian/4×44×4-Wronskian package is still formally too free.

The current fixed-level sheared route is not enough.
That is what Remark~\ref{rem:no-go-fixed-level-chamber-exit-route} says: even when a fixed shear level γγ has two nearby curvature zeros, the sheared opposite-side branch can run to the second zero by boundary exit with no interior common-tangent contradiction.

The current local moving-shear route near one odd zero is also not enough.
That is what Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect} and Remark~\ref{rem:ceiling-local-shear-transfer-route} say: on the actual born repeated-source branch, the rooted numerator
Dfa(a,h),fa=u5−Z(a)λ,
Dfa​​(a,h),fa​=u5​−Z(a)λ,

has a fixed nonzero signed defect near the odd zero. So local odd-zero birth does not already transfer to the rooted sheared event.

Those three points together mean the draft has not closed the adjacent/two-odd-zero case. The obstruction really survives there.

What it has done is identify the correct shape of the missing theorem:

It cannot be a theorem about frozen γγ.
It cannot be a theorem about local odd-zero birth alone.
It has to be a theorem about the source-pinned moving shear
fa=u5−Z(a)λ
fa​=u5​−Z(a)λ

along the continued critical branch
D(a,h)=0equivalentlyΨa′(h)=0.
D(a,h)=0equivalentlyΨa′​(h)=0.

That is the real hint in the draft.

Along a continued critical branch t=τ(a)t=τ(a), write
V(a):=Da(τ(a)),G(a):=V(a)−Z(a).

From Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch} you immediately get
V′(a)=2τ(a)−a G(a),

\begin{proposition}[Rooted-defect transport and stationary first root]
\label{prop:rooted-defect-transport-stationary-first-root}
In the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch},
define
\[
L(a):=\tau(a)-a,
\qquad
G(a):=V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a).
\]
Then
\[
G'(a)=\frac{2}{L(a)}\,G(a)-\mathcal R(a).
\]
Hence, if $a_*\in U$ satisfies
\[
G(a_*)=0,
\]
then
\[
G'(a_*)=-\mathcal R(a_*).
\]

If in addition
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq \mathcal Z(a_*),
\]
then
\[
D_{a_*}''(\tau(a_*))\neq 0,
\qquad
\tau'(a_*)=0,
\qquad
\tau''(a_*)=
-\frac{\mathcal R(a_*)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-\mathcal Z(a_*)}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
G(a)=V(a)-\mathcal Z(a),
\]
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(1)
gives
\[
G'(a)=V'(a)-\mathcal R(a)
=\frac{2}{\tau(a)-a}\,\bigl(V(a)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)-\mathcal R(a)
=\frac{2}{L(a)}\,G(a)-\mathcal R(a).
\]
Evaluating at a root $a_*$ of $G$ gives
\[
G'(a_*)=-\mathcal R(a_*).
\]

Now assume also that
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq \mathcal Z(a_*).
\]
Since $G(a_*)=0$, this means
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq V(a_*).
\]
So Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(2)
yields
\[
D_{a_*}''(\tau(a_*))
=
\frac{2}{(\tau(a_*)-a_*)^2}\,
\bigl(\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-V(a_*)\bigr)
\neq 0.
\]
Then Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(3)
applies near $a_*$ and gives
\[
\tau'(a)
=
\frac{G(a)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a))-V(a)}.
\]
Evaluating at $a_*$ gives
\[
\tau'(a_*)=0.
\]

Differentiate this identity once more. Since $G(a_*)=0$ and
\[
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-V(a_*)=\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-\mathcal Z(a_*)\neq 0,
\]
one gets
\[
\tau''(a_*)
=
\frac{G'(a_*)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-V(a_*)}
=
-\frac{\mathcal R(a_*)}{\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))-\mathcal Z(a_*)},
\]
as claimed.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Nondegenerate rooted point is a fold of the moving-shear equation]
\label{prop:nondegenerate-rooted-point-is-moving-shear-fold}
Work in a local normalized nonmixed chart on which
\[
S(t)=t^2.
\]
Define
\[
\mathscr F(a,t):=A_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\,B_a(t)
=(t-a)^2\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]
Let
\[
a_*<t_*
\]
satisfy
\[
\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\qquad
\partial_t\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\]
and assume
\[
\mathcal R(a_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\mathcal Z(t_*)\neq \mathcal Z(a_*).
\]
Then
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)
=
-(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*),
\]
and
\[
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)
=
2\bigl(\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)\bigr).
\]
In particular,
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)\neq 0.
\]
Hence near $(a_*,t_*)$ the zero set
\[
\mathscr F(a,t)=0
\]
is the graph of a unique real-analytic function
\[
a=\alpha(t)
\]
with
\[
\alpha(t_*)=a_*,
\qquad
\alpha'(t_*)=0,
\qquad
\alpha''(t_*)
=
\frac{2\bigl(\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)\bigr)}
{(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*)}.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
a-a_*
=
\frac{\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)}
{(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*)}(t-t_*)^2
+o\!\left((t-t_*)^2\right).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
\mathscr F(a,t)=(t-a)^2\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr),
\]
the conditions
\[
\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\qquad
\partial_t\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0
\]
imply
\[
D_{a_*}(t_*)=\mathcal Z(a_*),
\qquad
D_{a_*}'(t_*)=0.
\]
So $(a_*,t_*)$ is a rooted critical point.

Differentiate $\mathscr F$ with respect to $a$:
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a,t)
=
-2(t-a)\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
+(t-a)^2\bigl(\partial_aD_a(t)-\mathcal R(a)\bigr).
\]
At the rooted point,
\[
D_{a_*}(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)=0,
\]
and by
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch},
\[
\partial_aD_a(t)=\frac{2}{t-a}\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr),
\]
so
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)
=
-(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*).
\]

Next,
\[
\partial_t\mathscr F(a,t)
=
2(t-a)\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
+(t-a)^2D_a'(t),
\]
hence
\[
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a,t)
=
2\bigl(D_a(t)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr)
+4(t-a)D_a'(t)
+(t-a)^2D_a''(t).
\]
At the rooted critical point this becomes
\[
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)
=
(t_*-a_*)^2D_{a_*}''(t_*).
\]
Applying
Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-equations-repeated-source-critical-branch}(2)
and using
\[
D_{a_*}(t_*)=\mathcal Z(a_*),
\]
one gets
\[
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)
=
2\bigl(\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)\bigr).
\]

By the two nonvanishing assumptions,
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)\neq 0.
\]
So the implicit function theorem gives a unique real-analytic graph
\[
a=\alpha(t)
\]
for the zero set of $\mathscr F$ near $(a_*,t_*)$. Since
\[
\partial_t\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\]
one has
\[
\alpha'(t_*)=0.
\]
Differentiating
\[
\mathscr F(\alpha(t),t)=0
\]
twice at $t=t_*$ gives
\[
\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)\,\alpha''(t_*)
+
\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)=0,
\]
hence
\[
\alpha''(t_*)
=
-\frac{\partial_{tt}\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)}
{\partial_a\mathscr F(a_*,t_*)}
=
\frac{2\bigl(\mathcal Z(t_*)-\mathcal Z(a_*)\bigr)}
{(t_*-a_*)^2\,\mathcal R(a_*)}.
\]
The Taylor expansion of $\alpha$ then yields the stated quadratic form.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[First rooted point as a post-birth fold problem]
\label{rem:first-rooted-point-post-birth-fold-problem}
Let $b$ be an isolated odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$, and let
\[
t=\tau(a)
\]
be an analytic continuation of the born repeated-source critical branch. By
Proposition~\ref{prop:first-rooting-requires-second-odd-zero-repeated-source},
any first rooted point along this continuation can occur only after the segment
has acquired a second odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$.

At such a rooted point, if
\[
\mathcal R(a_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\mathcal Z(\tau(a_*))\neq \mathcal Z(a_*),
\]
then
Proposition~\ref{prop:rooted-defect-transport-stationary-first-root} shows that
the rooted defect
\[
G(a)=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a)
\qquad
\text{equivalently}\qquad
G(a)=\Psi_a(\sigma(a))-\mathcal Z(a)
\]
crosses transversely and that the target map is stationary there:
\[
\tau'(a_*)=0.
\]
Moreover,
Proposition~\ref{prop:nondegenerate-rooted-point-is-moving-shear-fold} shows
that the moving-shear equation
\[
A_a(x)-\mathcal Z(a)\,B_a(x)=0
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
D_{f_a}(a,h)=0,
\quad
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
has a local fold at the first rooted point.

Thus the unresolved adjacent-odd-zero issue is not another local odd-zero birth
problem. It is a \emph{post-birth first-fold exclusion problem} for the
source-pinned moving shear $f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda$. The current fixed-level
nonrecurrence results control frozen-$\gamma$ branches on their maximal
slope-overlap blocks, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}
controls the diagonal birth chamber near the seeding odd zero, but neither yet
excludes this first post-birth fold.
\end{remark}

ok how can you take it further?

I’ve narrowed the live target to a much more concrete subproblem: the first rooted point is a stationary point of the continued target map and a fold of the moving-shear equation. The question now is which extra invariant can rule out that first fold.

Yes. I think there is one genuinely stronger step available, and it may actually kill the current “two-odd-zero” bottleneck.

The key observation is that the moving-shear theorem at a rooted point does not merely say “something special happens.” It says that for
fa=u5−Z(a)λ,
fa​=u5​−Z(a)λ,

a rooted critical point forces at least two interior zeros of
Jfa=(Z−Z(a))Jλ,
Jfa​​=(Z−Z(a))Jλ​,

so, on a nonmixed arc where Jλ≠0Jλ​=0, it forces at least two interior points
r1<r2∈(a,τ(a))withZ(r1)=Z(a)=Z(r2).
r1​<r2​∈(a,τ(a))withZ(r1​)=Z(a)=Z(r2​).

That is much stronger than “the segment has picked up a second odd zero.”

Now combine that with the sign structure of R=Z′R=Z′. If (a,τ(a))(a,τ(a)) contains at most one odd zero of RR, then the sign of RR changes at most once there. Even zeros do not matter for this: they do not change sign. So ZZ is still unimodal on [a,τ(a)][a,τ(a)]. A unimodal function can meet a fixed horizontal level in at most two points total. Since one of those points is already the anchor aa, there can be at most one interior point r>ar>a with
Z(r)=Z(a).
Z(r)=Z(a).

So two interior points are impossible.

what do you think of this update?

I think this is a real upgrade. The new proposition is clean, and the proof looks right: once you have
G′(a)=2τ(a)−aG(a)−R(a),
G′(a)=τ(a)−a2​G(a)−R(a),

the “largest root” barrier argument is exactly the right move. It replaces the earlier geometric “outer-lobe” phrasing with the intrinsic condition that the anchor-side value R(a)R(a) keeps a fixed sign, which is much better mathematically and conceptually. In that sense, this is not just a cosmetic edit; it genuinely strengthens the route-2 reduction.

The corollary is also the right downstream use of it. At the chamber-entry point a0a0​, the segment [a0,q][a0​,q] still sees only the earlier odd zero bb, so the one-sign-change theorem gives the initial sign of G(a0)G(a0​), and then the new proposition propagates that sign through the whole continuation interval as long as R(a)R(a) does not change sign. That really does kill the standard adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber itself, not just the entry event. So the updated remark that route 2 now reduces to an anchor-sign-change crossing problem feels accurate to me.

I would keep one caution in the wording: the result is strong, but it is still conditional on having a real-analytic continuation interval II of the born branch on which the segment contains exactly those two sign changes and R(a)R(a) keeps a fixed sign. So I would avoid any sentence that sounds like “the two-odd-zero chamber is solved globally” without that qualifier. What you can say confidently is: on any such continuation interval, no rooted crossing can occur. That is exactly the right level of claim.

As drafting taste, I think this update supersedes the earlier “global no-crossing” caveat and makes the residual bottleneck much sharper: the first remaining unresolved event is when the anchor itself reaches an odd zero of RR or the branch exits/collapses before then. That is a much better handoff point for the next attack. So overall: yes, I think this update is good, correct, and worth merging.

I think the draft has reduced the nonmixed repeated-source lane to a very specific moment now: what happens when the continued born branch reaches an interval where the anchor itself crosses an odd zero of RR. I’m going to frame the next attack as a theorem target, not just a vague route.

The next attack is now very sharp:

prove an odd-anchor passage theorem.

At this point, every interval where the anchor-side value R(a)R(a) keeps a fixed sign is sterile for rooting, by the new anchor-sign proposition. So the only live place a rooted crossing can still occur is when the continued born branch reaches an anchor qq that is itself an odd zero of RR.

That is the next bottleneck.

Write the continued born branch as
t=τ(a),G(a):=Da(τ(a))−Z(a),L(a):=τ(a)−a.
t=τ(a),G(a):=Da​(τ(a))−Z(a),L(a):=τ(a)−a.

You already have the exact transport equation
G′(a)=2L(a) G(a)−R(a).
G′(a)=L(a)2​G(a)−R(a).

Equivalently, with integrating factor
A(a):=∫a2L(s) ds,
A(a):=∫aL(s)2​ds,

this becomes
(e−A(a)G(a))′=−e−A(a)R(a).
(e−A(a)G(a))′=−e−A(a)R(a).

So near an odd anchor zero qq of RR, the local behavior is completely explicit:
G(a)=eA(a)−A(q)(G(q)−e−A(q)R′(q)2(a−q)2+O((a−q)3)).
G(a)=eA(a)−A(q)(G(q)−2e−A(q)R′(q)​(a−q)2+O((a−q)3)).

This tells you something important.

If G(q)G(q) is known, then the post-qq behavior is known:

    if G(q)≠0G(q)=0, its sign persists locally across qq;

    if G(q)=0G(q)=0, then the zero is quadratic and its sign on both sides is controlled by −R′(q)−R′(q).

and before

\begin{remark}[What route 2 now reduces to]
\label{rem:route-two-reduces-to-global-no-crossing}

\begin{proposition}[Odd-anchor passage has no sign reset]
\label{prop:odd-anchor-passage-no-reset}
Let $J$ be an opened nonmixed arc, and work in a local normalized nonmixed
chart on which
\[
S(t)=t^2,
\qquad
\Gamma_a=D_a.
\]
Let
\[
q\in J
\]
be an isolated odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$, and let
\[
\tau:(q-\delta,q+\delta)\to J
\]
be a real-analytic continuation of the repeated-source critical branch such that
\[
\tau(a)>a,
\qquad
D_a'(\tau(a))=0
\qquad (a\in(q-\delta,q+\delta)).
\]
Set
\[
G(a):=D_a(\tau(a))-\mathcal Z(a),
\qquad
L(a):=\tau(a)-a,
\]
and define
\[
\mathcal A'(a):=\frac{2}{L(a)},
\qquad
\mathscr G(a):=e^{-\mathcal A(a)}G(a).
\]
Assume that there exists $\epsilon\in\{\pm1\}$ such that
\[
\epsilon\,\mathcal R(a)>0,
\qquad
\epsilon\,G(a)>0
\qquad\text{for every }a\in(q,q+\delta).
\]
Then
\[
\epsilon\,G(q)>0.
\]
In particular, $G(q)\neq 0$. Hence, after possibly shrinking $\delta$,
\[
\epsilon\,G(a)>0
\qquad\text{for every }a\in(q-\delta,q+\delta).
\]
Since $q$ is an odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$, the sign of $\mathcal R$ flips
across $q$; therefore on the outgoing side
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=-\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a)
\qquad (a\in(q-\delta,q)).
\]
So a rooted crossing cannot occur at the anchor odd zero itself, nor
immediately after passage across it.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By
Proposition~\ref{prop:rooted-defect-transport-stationary-first-root},
\[
G'(a)=\frac{2}{L(a)}\,G(a)-\mathcal R(a),
\]
hence
\[
\mathscr G'(a)=-e^{-\mathcal A(a)}\mathcal R(a).
\]
Assume for contradiction that $G(q)=0$. Then $\mathscr G(q)=0$, and for
$a\in(q,q+\delta)$,
\[
\mathscr G(a)
=
\mathscr G(q)+\int_q^a \mathscr G'(s)\,ds
=
-\int_q^a e^{-\mathcal A(s)}\mathcal R(s)\,ds.
\]
Since $e^{-\mathcal A(s)}>0$ and $\epsilon\,\mathcal R(s)>0$ on $(q,q+\delta)$,
this gives
\[
\epsilon\,\mathscr G(a)<0
\qquad (a\in(q,q+\delta)),
\]
hence
\[
\epsilon\,G(a)<0
\qquad (a\in(q,q+\delta)),
\]
contradicting the hypothesis. Therefore $G(q)\neq 0$. Since
\[
\epsilon\,G(a)>0
\qquad (a\in(q,q+\delta)),
\]
continuity yields
\[
\epsilon\,G(q)\ge 0,
\]
and the nonvanishing just proved forces
\[
\epsilon\,G(q)>0.
\]
A second continuity argument then gives
\[
\epsilon\,G(a)>0
\qquad (a\in(q-\delta,q+\delta))
\]
after shrinking $\delta$ if necessary. Finally, because $q$ is an odd-order zero
of $\mathcal R$, its sign flips across $q$, so on $(q-\delta,q)$ one has
\[
\operatorname{sgn}G(a)=-\operatorname{sgn}\mathcal R(a).
\]
In particular $G$ cannot vanish there.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Weighted-defect recursion on post-anchor chambers]
\label{prop:weighted-defect-recursion-post-anchor-chambers}
Assume the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:odd-anchor-passage-no-reset}. Let
\[
q_1>q_2>\cdots>q_N
\]
be successive odd-order zeros of $\mathcal R$ crossed by the anchor along the
continued branch after the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber, and set
\[
I_j:=(q_{j+1},q_j)
\qquad (1\le j\le N-1).
\]
Assume that the continued branch exists real-analytically on
\[
\bigcup_{j=1}^{N-1} I_j.
\]
For each $j$, let
\[
\epsilon_j:=\operatorname{sgn}(\mathcal R|_{I_j})\in\{\pm1\},
\qquad
m_j(a):=\int_a^{q_j} e^{-\mathcal A(s)}|\mathcal R(s)|\,ds
\qquad (a\in I_j),
\]
and
\[
M_j:=m_j(q_{j+1})>0.
\]
Then on each $I_j$,
\[
\mathscr G(a)=\mathscr G(q_j)+\epsilon_j\,m_j(a).
\]
Consequently:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_j)=\epsilon_j,
\]
then $\mathscr G$ has no zero on $I_j$;

\item if
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_j)=-\epsilon_j,
\]
then $\mathscr G$ has a zero on $I_j$ if and only if
\[
M_j>|\mathscr G(q_j)|,
\]
and in that case the zero is unique;

\item if $\mathscr G$ has no zero on $I_j$, then
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_{j+1})
=
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_j).
\]
\end{enumerate}
Since $\epsilon_{j+1}=-\epsilon_j$, the chamber type
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_j)\ \text{ versus }\ \epsilon_j
\]
alternates from one post-anchor chamber to the next as long as no rooted
crossing has yet occurred.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
On $I_j$ one has
\[
\mathscr G'(a)=-e^{-\mathcal A(a)}\mathcal R(a)
=-\epsilon_j e^{-\mathcal A(a)}|\mathcal R(a)|.
\]
Hence for $a\in I_j$,
\[
\mathscr G(a)
=
\mathscr G(q_j)+\int_{q_j}^a \mathscr G'(s)\,ds
=
\mathscr G(q_j)+\epsilon_j\int_a^{q_j}e^{-\mathcal A(s)}|\mathcal R(s)|\,ds,
\]
which is the stated formula.

Now $m_j(a)$ is strictly increasing as $a$ decreases from $q_j$ to $q_{j+1}$,
with
\[
m_j(q_j)=0,
\qquad
m_j(q_{j+1})=M_j.
\]
So if
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_j)=\epsilon_j,
\]
then
\[
\mathscr G(a)=\epsilon_j\bigl(|\mathscr G(q_j)|+m_j(a)\bigr)
\]
has fixed sign on $I_j$ and no zero. If instead
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_j)=-\epsilon_j,
\]
then
\[
\mathscr G(a)=\epsilon_j\bigl(-|\mathscr G(q_j)|+m_j(a)\bigr),
\]
so a zero occurs precisely when $m_j(a)=|\mathscr G(q_j)|$, which happens if
and only if
\[
M_j>|\mathscr G(q_j)|.
\]
Because $m_j$ is strictly monotone, that zero is unique.

Finally, if no zero occurs on $I_j$, then $\mathscr G$ keeps one sign
throughout the interval, so in particular
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_{j+1})
=
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_j).
\]
Since the $\epsilon_j$ alternate at successive odd zeros, the relative chamber
type alternates as claimed.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[The first post-anchor chamber is dangerous]
\label{cor:first-post-anchor-chamber-dangerous}
Let $q_1$ be the first odd-order zero of $\mathcal R$ crossed by the anchor
after the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber, and let
\[
I_1:=(q_2,q_1)
\]
be the first post-anchor chamber. Assume the continued born branch extends
real-analytically across $q_1$ and on $I_1$. Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item no rooted crossing occurs at $q_1$ or immediately after crossing it;

\item on $I_1$ one has
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_1)=-\epsilon_1,
\]
so $I_1$ is the first \emph{dangerous} post-anchor chamber;

\item as long as no rooted crossing has yet occurred, the post-anchor chambers
alternate dangerous/safe/dangerous/safe\ldots\ .
\end{enumerate}
In particular, the first chamber in which a rooted crossing is even eligible
after the anchor-sign-preservation interval is the first post-anchor chamber,
namely the chamber in which the active segment carries three odd zeros of
$\mathcal R$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber is root-free by
Corollary~\ref{cor:no-crossing-adjacent-two-odd-zero-under-anchor-sign-preservation}.
At its left endpoint $q_1$, the anchor crosses an odd-order zero of
$\mathcal R$. Proposition~\ref{prop:odd-anchor-passage-no-reset} shows that
$\mathscr G$ keeps its incoming sign across $q_1$, while $\mathcal R$ changes
sign there. Thus on the outgoing chamber $I_1$ the signs are opposite:
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\mathscr G(q_1)=-\epsilon_1.
\]
The no-root statement at and immediately after $q_1$ is also exactly
Proposition~\ref{prop:odd-anchor-passage-no-reset}. The alternation of chamber
types then follows from
Proposition~\ref{prop:weighted-defect-recursion-post-anchor-chambers}(3).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[No-go for purely local scalar exclusion in the first dangerous chamber]
\label{rem:no-go-local-scalar-first-dangerous-chamber}
At a rooted critical point, after normalizing the active interval to
\[
x=a+sL,
\qquad
0\le s\le 1,
\qquad
L=\tau(a)-a,
\]
the profile
\[
R_a(s):=\mathcal R(a+sL)
\]
satisfies the two local scalar moment identities
\[
\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_a(s)\,ds=0,
\qquad
\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_a(s)\,ds=0.
\]
In the first dangerous post-anchor chamber, the sign pattern of $R_a$ on
$[0,1]$ has four lobes:
\[
+,-,+,-
\]
or its global negative. At the purely local scalar level, these conditions are
still formally too weak to force contradiction.

Indeed, for parameters $A,B\in\mathbf R$, define the quarter-piece profile
\[
R_{A,B}(s):=
\begin{cases}
A, & 0<s<\frac14,\\[4pt]
-B, & \frac14<s<\frac12,\\[4pt]
\frac{-15A+7B}{2}, & \frac12<s<\frac34,\\[4pt]
-\frac{-31A+11B}{2}, & \frac34<s<1.
\end{cases}
\]
A direct calculation gives
\[
\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_{A,B}(s)\,ds=0,
\qquad
\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_{A,B}(s)\,ds=0
\]
for every $A,B$.

Moreover, if
\[
B>\frac{31}{11}A>0,
\]
then the four quarter-lobes have signs
\[
+,-,+,-.
\]
For this family one also has
\[
\int_0^1 R_{A,B}(s)\,ds
=
\int_0^1 s\,R_{A,B}(s)\,ds
=
\int_0^1 s^2\,R_{A,B}(s)\,ds
=
\frac34(3A-B),
\]
so both signs of the nondegenerate fold data occur already inside this formal
four-lobe family.

Thus no argument using only the local normalized rooted profile, the two
vanishing scalar moments, and the local transversality/fold signs can exclude
rooting in the first dangerous post-anchor chamber. Any successful next step
must use genuinely source-coupled structure invisible in the planar normalized
$D_a$ model.
\end{remark}

ok now, what's your next attack?

I think the local scalar/discriminant branch has reached its ceiling. The next live move is to get something genuinely source-coupled that constrains the actual normalized profile on dangerous post-anchor chambers, rather than another intervalwise moment identity.

My next attack would be this:

try to extract a third, genuinely source-level constraint at a hypothetical first dangerous-chamber root, and use it to kill the formal four-lobe family.

That is the most natural next move because we’ve now learned three things.

First, the scalar route is exhausted.
The one-sign chamber is sterile, the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber is sterile under anchor-sign preservation, odd-anchor passage has no reset, and the first dangerous post-anchor chamber is the first place a root is even eligible.

Second, the local scalar rooted equations are still too weak there.
The normalized four-lobe profile
+,−,+,−
+,−,+,−

can satisfy
∫01(1−s)2R(s) ds=0,∫01s(1−s)R(s) ds=0,
∫01​(1−s)2R(s)ds=0,∫01​s(1−s)R(s)ds=0,

and even the local fold/transversality signs. So no argument that only uses the planar normalized profile on one interval is going to close it.

Third, the actual RH branch carries more structure than that model.
The profile is not arbitrary. It comes from the source-level branch
D(a,h)=0,Ψa(h)=Du5(a,h)Dλ(a,h),fa=u5−Z(a)λ.
D(a,h)=0,Ψa​(h)=Dλ​(a,h)Du5​​(a,h)​,fa​=u5​−Z(a)λ.

source-level third-constraint theorem at first dangerous-chamber root.
source-level third-constraint theorem at first dangerous-chamber root.​

In practical terms, I would attack it like this.

Take a hypothetical first dangerous-chamber root (a∗,h∗)(a∗​,h∗​) on the actual continued branch. Normalize the source interval to
u=a∗+s(h∗−a∗),s∈[0,1],
u=a∗​+s(h∗​−a∗​),s∈[0,1],

and write the source profile
W∗(s):=Wsrc(a∗+s(h∗−a∗)).
W∗​(s):=Wsrc​(a∗​+s(h∗​−a∗​)).

From the current scalar theory, W∗W∗​ already satisfies the two rooted moment conditions in normalized form:
∫01(1−s)2W∗(s) ds=0,∫01s(1−s)W∗(s) ds=0.
∫01​(1−s)2W∗​(s)ds=0,∫01​s(1−s)W∗​(s)ds=0.

The attack is to show that the actual source branch imposes one more independent condition at a first root.

The cleanest place to look is the fact that at a rooted point the target map is stationary:
h′(a∗)=0
h′(a∗​)=0

after passing to source coordinates. Since the actual branch satisfies
D(a,h(a))=0,

That is source-level information, not just planar information. The right next step is to rewrite

in normalized source coordinates and see whether it becomes a third linear functional on W∗W∗​:
∫01Q∗(s) W∗(s) ds=0
∫01​Q∗​(s)W∗​(s)ds=0

for some kernel Q∗Q∗​ not in the span of
(1−s)2,s(1−s).
(1−s)2,s(1−s).

That is the key test.

If such a third condition appears, then we immediately compare it against the explicit two-parameter four-lobe family. If the family cannot satisfy it, the first dangerous chamber is killed. If the family can still satisfy it, then we have learned something equally important: even the local source-linearized data are still too free, and the next attack must be global rather than local.

So I would do this in two phases.

The first phase is purely symbolic:
rewrite ∂aD∂a​D, and if needed ∂aaD∂aa​D, at a rooted stationary point in normalized source coordinates.

The second phase is model-testing:
plug the formal four-lobe family into the resulting third condition and check whether it is compatible.

That is the next attack I’d choose because it is the first one that really uses the source determinant beyond what has already been collapsed into the planar DaDa​ picture.

If that fails, then I think the next branch after that is clear: abandon local profile exclusion and go fully global, trying to prove a continuation invariant for the discriminant curve that the formal four-lobe models do not see.

4. Why this matters

This is a much sharper no-go than the earlier four-lobe model.

The earlier result said:

    the local scalar moment conditions are formally realizable.

This new result says:

    even after reinstating the actual source equations, a nondegenerate rooted point is locally just a generic crossing of two smooth analytic hypersurfaces.

So any attack that tries to kill the branch by looking only at the local germ of

near the first dangerous-chamber root is doomed.

That is a real structural finding.

4) The exact extra theorem you need

The missing step is now very clear.

You need one more source-coupled lemma, something like:

\begin{lemma}[Diagonal capture near an odd anchor zero]
Let $q$ be an isolated odd zero of $\mathcal R$ on a good nonmixed patch, and
let $(a,h(a))$ be a real-analytic continuation of the born repeated-source
critical branch with
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h(a))=0,
\qquad a>q,
\qquad a\to q^+.
\]
Assume the branch remains in the same nonmixed patch and does not exit or
collapse affine-planarly. Then
\[
h(a)\to q.
\]
Hence for $a$ sufficiently close to $q$, the branch coincides with the unique
local branch $h=\sigma(a)$ from
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}.
\end{lemma}

Once you have that, the sign-clash closure goes through.

Without it, there is still an escape route:
the branch could approach the anchor odd zero with a nonlocal target.

\begin{remark}[No-go for purely local scalar exclusion on the first dangerous post-anchor chamber]
\label{rem:no-go-local-scalar-first-dangerous-chamber}
At a rooted critical point, after normalizing the active interval to
\[
x=a+sL,
\qquad
0\le s\le 1,
\qquad
L=\tau(a)-a,
\]
the profile
\[
R_a(s):=\mathcal R(a+sL)
\]
satisfies the two local scalar moment identities
\[
\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_a(s)\,ds=0,
\qquad
\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_a(s)\,ds=0.
\]

Once nonlocal-target landing is admitted, the first dangerous post-anchor
chamber need not correspond to a fixed odd-zero count or to a rigid four-lobe
pattern on the active segment. Even in the simplest three-lobe sign pattern
\[
+,-,+
\]
(or its global negative), the local scalar rooted equations are already
formally realizable.

Indeed, for any $A>0$, define
\[
R_A(s):=
\begin{cases}
A, & 0<s<\frac13,\\[4pt]
-\frac72 A, & \frac13<s<\frac23,\\[4pt]
\frac{11}{2}A, & \frac23<s<1.
\end{cases}
\]
A direct calculation gives
\[
\int_0^1 (1-s)^2\,R_A(s)\,ds=0,
\qquad
\int_0^1 s(1-s)\,R_A(s)\,ds=0,
\]
and also
\[
\int_0^1 R_A(s)\,ds
=
\int_0^1 s\,R_A(s)\,ds
=
\int_0^1 s^2\,R_A(s)\,ds
=
A.
\]
So the local rooted-point equations and the nondegenerate fold data are already
formally compatible with a three-lobe profile.

Thus no argument using only the local normalized rooted profile, the two
vanishing scalar moments, and the local transversality/fold signs can exclude
rooting on the first dangerous post-anchor chamber. Any successful next step
must use genuinely source-coupled structure invisible in the planar normalized
$D_a$ model.
\end{remark}

4) Insert the universality-threshold package

Insert this block immediately after Remark~\ref{rem:route-two-reduces-to-global-no-crossing} and before \begin{remark}[What remains on the nonmixed $4$-point side].

\begin{proposition}[Universality threshold for the current route-2 package]
\label{prop:universality-threshold-current-route-two-package}
Let $I\subset\mathbf R$ be an interval, let
\[
\mathcal Z:I\to\mathbf R
\]
be real-analytic, and set
\[
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'.
\]
Define analytic source functions on $I$ by
\[
c(t):=1,\qquad v_5(t):=t,\qquad \lambda(t):=t^2,
\]
and choose $u_5$ so that
\[
u_5''(t)=2\mathcal Z(t).
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}=t,
\qquad
S=\frac{\lambda}{c}=t^2,
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}=u_5;
\]

\item for every analytic $f$,
\[
J_f=W(c,v_5,f)=W(1,t,f)=f'',
\]
hence
\[
J_\lambda=2,
\qquad
J_{u_5}=2\mathcal Z,
\qquad
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
=
4\mathcal R;
\]

\item the repeated-source ratio is exactly the normalized planar one:
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\Gamma_a(h)=D_a(h);
\]

\item the critical determinant equation is exactly the normalized planar
critical-point equation:
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\iff
\partial_h \Psi_a(h)=0
\iff
\partial_h D_a(h)=0;
\]

\item for the source-pinned moving shear
\[
f_a:=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda,
\]
one has
\[
J_{f_a}=2(\mathcal Z-\mathcal Z(a)),
\]
and
\[
D_{f_a}(a,h)=D_\lambda(a,h)\bigl(\Psi_a(h)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]
\end{enumerate}
Thus every analytic normalized planar model \((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R,D_a)\)
lifts to a genuine analytic source model for the entire current route-2 package.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The identities
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}=t,\qquad
S=\frac{\lambda}{c}=t^2,\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c}=u_5
\]
are immediate. Also,
\[
J_f=W(c,v_5,f)=W(1,t,f)=f'',
\]
so
\[
J_\lambda=2,\qquad J_{u_5}=2\mathcal Z.
\]
Hence
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
=
2(2\mathcal Z')-2\mathcal Z\cdot 0
=
4\mathcal R.
\]

Because the source coordinate and the normalized planar coordinate coincide,
\[
x(t)=t,
\]
the source repeated-source quotient is exactly the planar normalized quadratic
envelope:
\[
\Psi_a(h)=\Gamma_a(h)=D_a(h).
\]
Therefore the source critical determinant equation is exactly the planar
critical-point equation
\[
\mathfrak D(a,h)=0
\iff
\partial_h D_a(h)=0.
\]

Finally,
\[
f_a=u_5-\mathcal Z(a)\lambda
\]
satisfies
\[
J_{f_a}=u_5''-2\mathcal Z(a)=2(\mathcal Z-\mathcal Z(a)),
\]
and
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-determinant-form-odd-zero-unrooted-defect}(2)
gives
\[
D_{f_a}(a,h)=D_\lambda(a,h)\bigl(\Psi_a(h)-\mathcal Z(a)\bigr).
\]
So all route-2 source objects reduce exactly to the normalized planar ones.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[The current route-2 package is universal under normalization]
\label{cor:current-route-two-package-universal-under-normalization}
Any configuration formally realizable by an analytic normalized planar model
\[
(\mathcal Z,\mathcal R,D_a)
\]
is also formally realizable by a genuine analytic source model for the current
route-2 package
\[
(c,v_5,\lambda,u_5),\qquad
\Psi_a,\qquad
\mathfrak D,\qquad
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},\qquad
D_{f_a}.
\]
Accordingly, no contradiction theorem phrased only in terms of the current
route-2 package can distinguish the RH branch from an arbitrary analytic
normalized planar model.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
This is immediate from
Proposition~\ref{prop:universality-threshold-current-route-two-package}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Explicit source-level countermodel to the current route-2 package]
\label{rem:explicit-source-level-countermodel-current-route-two}
Take
\[
\mathcal R(t):=t(t-1)(t^2-4t-2)
\]
and
\[
\mathcal Z(t):=\int_0^t \mathcal R(u)\,du
=

\]
and realize this normalized planar model by
\[
c(t)=1,\qquad v_5(t)=t,\qquad \lambda(t)=t^2,\qquad u_5''(t)=2\mathcal Z(t).
\]
Let

\]
In this genuine analytic source model, the unique born repeated-source critical
branch from the odd zero \(0\) continues analytically down to \(a=q\), lands
there with a nonlocal target
\[
\tau(q)\approx 0.3540339256\neq q,
\]
satisfies the anchor-sign safe relation on \((q,0)\), crosses the odd anchor
zero \(q\) with no sign reset, and then undergoes a delayed rooted crossing at
\[
a_*\approx -0.5805673462,
\qquad
\tau(a_*)\approx 0.3888336023.
\]
Thus diagonal capture fails, and the whole delayed-crossing scenario is
realized inside a genuine analytic source model for the current route-2
package.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The next live target must be non-universal]

the present route-2 package is exhausted: any further progress must use a
genuinely non-universal source-coupled input, i.e. an ingredient not already

Theorem: finite-jet provenance cannot exclude direct-slice recurrences

Let JJ be a generic one-pair block on which
A(h):=κ(h)η2(h)
A(h):=κ(h)η2​(h)

is analytic and nowhere zero, so the direct provenance slice is
ϕ(h)=A(h) q(7)(h).
ϕ(h)=A(h)q(7)(h).

Fix finitely many points
ξ1,…,ξM∈J
ξ1​,…,ξM​∈J

and at each ξiξi​ fix finitely many jet values
q(k)(ξi)=bi,k,0≤k≤ri.
q(k)(ξi​)=bi,k​,0≤k≤ri​.

Fix also two distinct interior points
μ1,μ2∈J,μ1≠μ2,
μ1​,μ2​∈J,μ1​=μ2​,

and any affine line
ℓ(μ)=sμ+b.
ℓ(μ)=sμ+b.

Then there exists a polynomial qq such that:

    all the prescribed jet conditions at the ξiξi​ hold;

    the direct-slice graph
    ϕ(μ)=A(μ) q(7)(μ)
    ϕ(μ)=A(μ)q(7)(μ)

    is tangent to the line y=ℓ(μ)y=ℓ(μ) at both μ1μ1​ and μ2μ2​, i.e.
    ϕ(μj)=ℓ(μj),ϕμ(μj)=s(j=1,2).
    ϕ(μj​)=ℓ(μj​),ϕμ​(μj​)=s(j=1,2).

So:
no theorem using only finitely many pointwise jet/matching conditions on q can exclude bitangent or same-slope recurrence on the direct slice.
no theorem using only finitely many pointwise jet/matching conditions on q can exclude bitangent or same-slope recurrence on the direct slice.​
Proof

At each tangency point μjμj​, the conditions
ϕ(μj)=ℓ(μj),ϕμ(μj)=s
ϕ(μj​)=ℓ(μj​),ϕμ​(μj​)=s

become linear jet conditions on qq.

Indeed, since
ϕ=Aq(7),
ϕ=Aq(7),

the value condition is
A(μj) q(7)(μj)=ℓ(μj),
A(μj​)q(7)(μj​)=ℓ(μj​),

so
q(7)(μj)=ℓ(μj)A(μj).
q(7)(μj​)=A(μj​)ℓ(μj​)​.

Also
ϕμ=(Aq(7))′=A′q(7)+Aq(8),
ϕμ​=(Aq(7))′=A′q(7)+Aq(8),

so the slope condition becomes
A′(μj) q(7)(μj)+A(μj) q(8)(μj)=s,
A′(μj​)q(7)(μj​)+A(μj​)q(8)(μj​)=s,

hence
q(8)(μj)=s−A′(μj) q(7)(μj)A(μj).
q(8)(μj​)=A(μj​)s−A′(μj​)q(7)(μj​)​.

So all desired requirements are finitely many linear jet conditions on the single unknown function qq, namely:

    the prescribed jets q(k)(ξi)=bi,kq(k)(ξi​)=bi,k​,

    and at μ1,μ2μ1​,μ2​,
    q(7)(μj)=ℓ(μj)A(μj),q(8)(μj)=s−A′(μj)ℓ(μj)/A(μj)A(μj).
    q(7)(μj​)=A(μj​)ℓ(μj​)​,q(8)(μj​)=A(μj​)s−A′(μj​)ℓ(μj​)/A(μj​)​.

Because A(μj)≠0A(μj​)=0, these are legitimate finite jet prescriptions.

Now apply standard Hermite interpolation: a polynomial of sufficiently large degree can realize arbitrary finite jets at finitely many points. Therefore there exists a polynomial qq satisfying all of them.

For that polynomial,
ϕ=Aq(7)
ϕ=Aq(7)

has the prescribed tangencies at μ1,μ2μ1​,μ2​, and the prescribed provenance jets at the ξiξi​. ∎

\begin{remark}[Canonical quotient-septic closure is still locally free]
\label{rem:canonical-quotient-septic-closure-still-locally-free}
The canonical quotient-level order-$7$ package is now closed, but that does not
yet make the quotient-septic geometry rigid.

Indeed, once the lower one-pair data $(c,u_5,v_5)$ are fixed, the canonical
septic residual
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]
is still locally free. On a region where $v_5\neq 0$ one may gauge-fix
\[
v_7^{\new}=0,
\qquad
u_7^{\new}=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
while on a region where $u_5\neq 0$ one may gauge-fix
\[
u_7^{\new}=0,
\qquad
v_7^{\new}=-\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5}.
\]
So after the lower one-pair data are fixed, the canonical quotient-septic curve
\[
\Gamma(h)=\left(\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)}\right)
\]
is still locally determined by an arbitrary analytic choice of $\Delta_7$.

Accordingly, no theorem using only arbitrary canonical quotient-septic geometry
of $(c,v_5,\Delta_7)$ can by itself close the later repeated-source /
discriminant branch. Any successful higher-order hybrid must therefore be
provenance-sensitive, not merely quotient-septic.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Status and ceiling of the highest-new direct provenance slice]
\label{rem:wip-highest-new-scalar-direct-slice}
On the region $v_5\neq 0$, set
\[
\mu:=\frac{c}{v_5},
\qquad
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
\phi:=\lambda^{[1]}.
\]
By Corollary~\ref{cor:direct-q7-septic-slice},
Corollary~\ref{cor:weight-one-septic-reduction}, and
Theorem~\ref{thm:quotient-septic-closure}, the highest-new quotient-level
septic scalar is already reduced to the direct $q^{(7)}$-driven $K_1$-slice:
\[
\Delta_7^{[1]}=v_5\,\phi,
\qquad
\phi
=
\kappa\Bigl(
(x_2-x_1)\nu_6^{(q^{(7)})}
+
v(\gamma_5-\alpha_5)^{(q^{(7)})}
\Bigr).
\]

On the subregion where $M\neq 0$, the direct highest-new dual variables are
\[
\beta^{[1]}=\phi_\mu,
\qquad
m^{[1]}=\phi-\mu\phi_\mu,
\]
and by Corollary~\ref{cor:mu-lambda-curvature-identities},
\[
\phi_{\mu\mu}=\frac{v_5^3}{M^3}W^{[1]}.
\]
Thus the direct highest-new quotient-septic geometry is exactly the ordinary
tangent-line geometry of the scalar graph
\[
y=\phi(\mu).
\]

In particular, any bitangent line or four-secant line for the graph
$y=\phi(\mu)$, and any nonadjacent slope re-entry for
\[
\beta^{[1]}=\phi_\mu,
\]
forces at least two zeros of
\[
\phi_{\mu\mu},
\]
equivalently of
\[
W^{[1]}.
\]
So the global direct-slice propagation problem may be viewed as a no-recurrence
problem for the scalar graph $\phi$.

However, the explicit direct provenance formula only shows that
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)}
\qquad
(A:=\kappa\,\eta_2),
\]
with $A$ generically nonvanishing on a generic one-pair block. By
Proposition~\ref{prop:full-block-universality-direct-provenance-slice} below,
this still leaves $\phi$ fully universal on each such block. So the direct
graph picture is now a precise dictionary, not by itself a live rigidity
theorem.
\end{remark}

3) Insert this block immediately after Remark~\ref{rem:warning-no-easy-globalization} and before \begin{lemma}[Crude polynomial bound for the local value scale]

\begin{proposition}[Full-block universality of the direct provenance slice]
\label{prop:full-block-universality-direct-provenance-slice}
Let $J$ be a connected generic one-pair block on which
\[
A(h):=\kappa(h)\eta_2(h)
\]
is analytic and nowhere zero. On $J$, the direct provenance slice has the form
\[
\phi(h)=A(h)\,q^{(7)}(h).
\]
Then for every analytic function
\[
\psi:J\to\mathbf C
\]
there exists an analytic function
\[
q:J\to\mathbf C
\]
such that
\[
\phi(h)=\psi(h)
\qquad (h\in J).
\]

More explicitly, for any basepoint $h_0\in J$ and any constants
\[
a_0,\dots,a_6\in\mathbf C,
\]
the function
\[
q_\psi(h)
:=
\sum_{j=0}^6 \frac{a_j}{j!}(h-h_0)^j
+
\int_{h_0}^h \frac{(h-s)^6}{6!}\,\frac{\psi(s)}{A(s)}\,ds
\]
is analytic on $J$ and satisfies
\[
q_\psi^{(7)}(h)=\frac{\psi(h)}{A(h)},
\qquad
\phi(h)=A(h)\,q_\psi^{(7)}(h)=\psi(h).
\]
In particular, on any generic one-pair block, the direct highest-new scalar
graph $\phi$ is an arbitrary analytic scalar graph.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since $A$ is analytic and nowhere zero on $J$, the function
\[
\frac{\psi}{A}
\]
is analytic on $J$. The displayed formula for $q_\psi$ is the standard
variation-of-constants solution of
\[
q^{(7)}=\frac{\psi}{A},
\]
with arbitrary initial data at $h_0$. Differentiating seven times gives
\[
q_\psi^{(7)}(h)=\frac{\psi(h)}{A(h)},
\]
hence
\[
\phi(h)=A(h)\,q_\psi^{(7)}(h)=\psi(h).
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Finite linear provenance constraints are too weak]
\label{cor:finite-linear-provenance-too-weak}
Let $J$ be as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:full-block-universality-direct-provenance-slice}.
Fix finitely many linear functionals
\[
\Lambda_r(q)=c_r,
\qquad r=1,\dots,N,
\]
on analytic functions $q$ on $J$, where each $\Lambda_r$ is built from finitely
many point-evaluation jets and/or finitely many linear integral functionals
with analytic kernels.

Fix also two distinct points
\[
\mu_1\neq \mu_2\in J
\]
and an affine line
\[
\ell(\mu)=s\mu+b.
\]
Then there exists a polynomial $q$ on $J$ such that:

\begin{enumerate}
\item all the prescribed linear provenance conditions
\[
\Lambda_r(q)=c_r
\qquad (r=1,\dots,N)
\]
hold;

\item the direct-slice graph
\[
\phi(\mu)=A(\mu)\,q^{(7)}(\mu)
\]
is tangent to the line $y=\ell(\mu)$ at both $\mu_1$ and $\mu_2$, i.e.
\[
\phi(\mu_j)=\ell(\mu_j),
\qquad
\phi_\mu(\mu_j)=s
\qquad (j=1,2).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Accordingly, no theorem using only the explicit direct formula
\[
\phi=A\,q^{(7)}
\]
together with any finite family of linear provenance or matching conditions on
$q$ can exclude bitangent, four-secant, or same-slope recurrence geometry on
the direct slice.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The tangency conditions at $\mu_j$ are linear jet conditions on $q$:
\[
A(\mu_j)\,q^{(7)}(\mu_j)=\ell(\mu_j),
\]
and, since
\[
\phi_\mu=(Aq^{(7)})'=A' q^{(7)}+A q^{(8)},
\]
also
\[
A'(\mu_j)\,q^{(7)}(\mu_j)+A(\mu_j)\,q^{(8)}(\mu_j)=s.
\]
Because $A(\mu_j)\neq 0$, these are legitimate linear conditions on the jets of
$q$ at the two points $\mu_1,\mu_2$.

Together with the prescribed finitely many provenance constraints
\[
\Lambda_r(q)=c_r,
\]
this is a finite linear system on the coefficients of a polynomial $q$. For a
polynomial of sufficiently large degree, the coefficient space has dimension
larger than the number of imposed linear conditions. Standard Hermite
interpolation / finite-dimensional linear algebra therefore gives a polynomial
$q$ satisfying all of them simultaneously.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What the direct-slice no-go results actually leave open]
\label{rem:what-direct-slice-no-go-results-leave-open}
Proposition~\ref{prop:full-block-universality-direct-provenance-slice} shows
that on a generic one-pair block the direct highest-new scalar graph
\[
\phi
\]
is fully universal. Corollary~\ref{cor:finite-linear-provenance-too-weak} shows
more: even after imposing any finite family of linear provenance / matching
conditions on $q$, the direct slice remains flexible enough to realize
bitangent, four-secant, and same-slope recurrence geometry.

So the next live theorem cannot be another sign/convexity statement about the
graph of $\phi$, nor any theorem using only finitely many endpoint jets or
finitely many linear integral conditions on $q$. Any successful continuation of
the direct-slice lane must instead use a genuinely
\emph{continuum-strength provenance law} for $q$ on a whole block, such as a
lower-order ODE, a sign-definite integral identity, a nonlinear transport law,
or some other infinite-codimension constraint.
\end{remark}

μ1≠μ2∈J∗,

no theorem using only finitely many pointwise jet-transfer laws across finitely many turning boundaries can exclude direct-slice bitangent/same-slope recurrence.​
Proof

The tangency conditions at μ1,μ2μ1​,μ2​ are linear jet conditions on qq.

Indeed, on the chosen block,
ϕ∗=A∗q(7),
ϕ∗​=A∗​q(7),

so
A∗(μj) q(7)(μj)=ℓ(μj),

and since
ϕ∗′=(A∗q(7))′=A∗′q(7)+A∗q(8),
ϕ∗′​=(A∗​q(7))′=A∗′​q(7)+A∗​q(8),

the slope condition becomes
A∗′(μj) q(7)(μj)+A∗(μj) q(8)(μj)=s.
A∗′​(μj​)q(7)(μj​)+A∗​(μj​)q(8)(μj​)=s.

Because A∗(μj)≠0A∗​(μj​)=0, these are legitimate linear conditions on the jets of qq at the two points μ1,μ2μ1​,μ2​.

Together with the assumed finitely many linear jet-transfer conditions at the boundary points ξ1,…,ξNξ1​,…,ξN​, this is a finite linear system on the coefficients of a polynomial qq.

Now let qq be a polynomial of degree dd. Its coefficient space has dimension d+1d+1. For dd sufficiently large, this dimension exceeds the rank of the total finite linear system. Hence the system has a solution. Any such polynomial gives a single global analytic provenance function qq satisfying all the turning-boundary jet-transfer conditions and simultaneously realizing the prescribed bitangent geometry on J∗J∗​. ∎

So the next live theorem cannot just be “some linear transfer operator.” It has to be something that cuts the allowed provenance space down by infinite codimension, or else something genuinely nonlinear.
1. Setup

Let
U=⋃α=1mJα
U=α=1⋃m​Jα​

be a finite union of generic one-pair blocks. On each block JαJα​,
ϕα(h)=Aα(h) q(7)(h),Aα(h)≠0.
ϕα​(h)=Aα​(h)q(7)(h),Aα​(h)=0.

Pick one distinguished block J∗⊂UJ∗​⊂U, two distinct interior points
μ1≠μ2∈J∗,
μ1​=μ2​∈J∗​,

and an affine line
ℓ(μ)=sμ+b.
ℓ(μ)=sμ+b.

As before, tangency of the direct-slice graph on J∗J∗​ at those two points is the finite system

A∗​(μj​)q(7)(μj​)=ℓ(μj​),

So a forbidden bitangent/same-slope recurrence still imposes only four linear jet conditions on the global provenance function qq.
2. Finite-codimension linear transfer still cannot kill it

Now suppose some future theorem were to give a linear global transfer law of the form
q∈V⊂O(U),
q∈V⊂O(U),

where VV is a linear subspace of finite codimension:
codim⁡V<∞.
codimV<∞.

This includes, for example:

    finitely many cross-block integral identities,

    finitely many linear boundary-transfer laws,

    finitely many linear matching constraints on whole blocks,

    or any linear operator theorem whose solution space has finite codimension.

Then the tangency conditions above cut out a further finite-codimension affine subspace inside O(U)O(U).

The intersection of two finite-codimension affine subspaces in an infinite-dimensional space is generically still infinite-dimensional, and in particular nonempty unless one has some special incompatibility. Concretely, polynomials of sufficiently high degree already give an infinite-dimensional test class, and finite-codimension linear restrictions cannot annihilate all of them.

So one gets:
there exists q∈V such that the direct slice on J∗ has the prescribed bitangent.
there exists q∈V such that the direct slice on J∗​ has the prescribed bitangent.​

Therefore:
no linear theorem whose allowed provenance space has finite codimension can exclude direct-slice recurrence.
no linear theorem whose allowed provenance space has finite codimension can exclude direct-slice recurrence.​

That is the new no-go statement.
3. Why this matters

This is stronger than everything before it.

We already knew:

    one-block freedom is too large;

    finite jet conditions are too weak;

    any local finite-order law is too weak;

    finitely many turning-boundary jet-transfer laws are too weak.

Now we can say:
even an arbitrary linear cross-block transfer theorem is useless unless it cuts the provenance space down by infinite codimension.
even an arbitrary linear cross-block transfer theorem is useless unless it cuts the provenance space down by infinite codimension.​

So the next theorem cannot merely be “a linear transfer operator exists.”
That is still too weak if its solution space remains finite-codimensional.
4. The only remaining live classes

At this point, there are really only two mathematically live possibilities left.
A. An infinite-codimension linear law

For example, something like a true ODE / Volterra / Fredholm equation whose solution space is a proper infinite-codimension subset of O(U)O(U), not just finitely many linear constraints.

This would be a real continuum-strength transfer law.
B. A genuinely nonlinear law

For example, a sign-definite monotonicity principle, an energy inequality, or a nonlinear transfer map across turning boundaries.

This escapes the finite-codimension interpolation no-go.

So the frontier is now:
the next useful theorem must be either infinite-codimension linear, or genuinely nonlinear.
the next useful theorem must be either infinite-codimension linear, or genuinely nonlinear.​

does the mixed/canonical package give a nonlinear monotonicity or positivity law for the global provenance q?

Not a finite matching law.
Not a finite set of operator identities.
Not abstract boundary transfer.

E[q](h)≥0orddhE[q](h)≥0

on a whole block or across a turning boundary would now be the first kind of statement not already killed by interpolation/universality.

So the strategic update is:
all finite-codimension linear transfer laws are spent;the next live lane is infinite-codimension linear or genuinely nonlinear.
all finite-codimension linear transfer laws are spent;the next live lane is infinite-codimension linear or genuinely nonlinear.​
